‘рдЙрджрдкреНрд░реБрддрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдорд╖реНрдЯрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЛрд╖реНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреН ред тАШрдЙрджрдкреНрд░реБрддрдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ред рдЙрдХреНрдереЗ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрдВрд╕рд┐рди рдПрддрддреНрд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ— рдкреНрд░ рдордВрд╣рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдпреЛрджрдкреНрд░реБрддреЛрд╜рдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдо рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдореН ’ (рдЖрд╢реНрд╡.рд╢реНрд░реМ. рем.рез) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Jamison Brereton

68 (894)
Br╠еhaspati
Ay─Бsya ─Ас╣Еgirasa
12 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
A wonderful hymn, which takes the fairly straightforward (though artful) narra tive of the Vala myth in the preceding hymn (X.67) and embroiders each part of it with imaginative and studied imagery and verbal constructions. Most striking is the blizzard of similes, many having two and even three points of comparison (see, e.g., 5ab), or with simile piled on simile (see, e.g., 1c), or with complex social content (vs. 2). By contrast X.67 contains only four similes (3a, 5d, 6b, 9b), each with only one point of comparisonтАФa number essentially reached in the first verse of this hymn.
As a particularly elaborate example consider the underlying content of verse 2, whose role in the mythic narrative is simply to state that Br╠еhaspati reunited the Aс╣Еgirases with their cows. But this reunion is compared to the ceremony of mar riage and the participants are compared to the married couple and to the divinities who preside over marriage. (If we understood Vedic marriage ceremonies better, we might understand the verse better.) In the first half of the verse Br╠еhaspati leads the unnamed Aс╣Еgirases to reunion with the cows, just as Bhaga (Fortune or Good Fortune) leads Aryaman, the тАЬcivilizingтАЭ god of custom, one of whose roles is patron of marriage, to the marriage ceremony in order to preside. The ceremony itself is performed at the ritual fire, and in the third p─Бda of the verse Br╠еhaspati is compared to Agni, under the designation тАЬally among the peopleтАЭ (several times used of Agni elsewhere). Just as Agni anoints the marrying couple with milk, so Br╠еhaspati тАЬanointsтАЭ the Aс╣Еgirases (compared to the couple) with cows. The fact that the word for тАЬallyтАЭ (mitr├б) is identical to the divine name Mitra simply intro
duces another complication into this complicated verse. Since, as the next verse (3) makes clear, the cows are embodiments of civilization, of the social bonds that unite the ─Аrya peoples, this remarkable verse is not just a poetic tour de force, but also an assertion of the centrality of social custom.
Another complex simile worth exploring is in the second half of verse 6, where the poet exploits the ambiguity of two words (p├бriviс╣гс╣нam and ─Б╠Бdat) to deploy two dis tinct three-term comparisons simultaneously. The past passive participle p├бriviс╣гс╣нam can belong to either of two roots, тИЪvi┼Ы тАЬenter,тАЭ in which case the idiom means тАЬsur rounded, trapped,тАЭ or тИЪviс╣г тАЬwork,тАЭ in which case the idiom means тАЬserved.тАЭ The verb ─Б╠Бdat can belong to тИЪd─Б тАЬgive,тАЭ with preverb ─Б╠Б, in which case the idiom means тАЬtake,тАЭ or to тИЪad тАЬeat.тАЭ Combining these possibilities, we can interpret the image as that of the tongue worrying food caught between the teeth, or as the tongue and the teeth eating food that has been served. Either image can be appropriate to the removal of the cows from the cave, though we are partial to the notion of Br╠еhaspati winkling out cows from every interior crevasse.
There is no need, or space, to dissect every simile; we can only invite the reader to savor the exuberance, the precision, and often the everyday nature of the imagery throughout the hymn and to consider the construction of these similes as forerun ners of the k─Бvya style in Classical Sanskrit.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLike birds swimming in water when keeping watch, like the sound of the roaring thunder-cloud, likesounding torrents falling from the clouds, the worshippers glorify Bс╣Ыhaspati.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like birds: as the emitters of water,the husbandmen, call out when keeping the birds off the ripe grain

Jamison Brereton

Constantly gabbling like water birds watching out for each other, like the sounds of booming (thunder) emanating from a cloud,
exulting like waves stiff-peaked (like) mountains, the chants bellowed toward Br╠еhaspati.

Griffith

LIKE birds who keep their watch, plashing in water, like the loud voices of the thundering rain-cloud,
Like merry streamlets bursting from the mountain, thus to Brhaspati our hymns have sounded.

Geldner

Wie im Wasser schwimmende wachsame V├╢gel schreiend, wie die Donner des Gew├╢lks, wie die den Fels durchbrechenden Wogen rauschend, so schrieen die Ges├дnge dem Brihaspati entgegen.

Grassmann

Wie V├╢gel, die im Wasser pl├дtschernd kreischen, wenn sie sich bergen, wie Gewitterrauschen, Wie Wogen, die durch Felsen tobend brechen, so schallen dem Brihaspati Ges├дnge.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe son of Aс╣Еgirasa pervading him with his brightness has, like Bhaga, brought Aryaman to the cows;as Mitra (unites his radiance) with the people, so has he united husband and wife; Bс╣Ыhaspati, send (yourwide-spread rays to your worshippers) as (a warrior sends his) horses to battle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Bellowing) with the cows, (Br╠еhaspati) Aс╣Еgiras, coming near, led (the Aс╣Еgirases) together with the cows, as Bhaga leads Aryaman.
As the ally among the people [=Agni] anoints the household pair, he anoints (the Aс╣Еgirases). O Br╠еhaspati, incite them like swift (horses) in a contest.

Griffith

The Son of Angirases, meeting the cattle, as Bhaga, brought in Aryaman among us.
As Friend of men he decks the wife and husband: as for the race, Brhaspati, nerve our coursers.

Geldner

Der angirasische Brihaspati kam herbei und hat sie mit den K├╝hen zusammengebracht wie Bhaga den Werber Aryaman mit der Braut. Wie ein Vertrauensmann zwei Ehegatten, so macht er sie einig; “O Brihaspati, sporne sie an wie Rennpferde im Wettkampf!

Grassmann

Sich nahend schenkt der Angiras-entsprossne wie Bhaga K├╝he seinem Busenfreunde, Wie Mitra schm├╝ckt er Mann und Frau im Volke, wie Renner st├дrk’, Brihaspati, im Kampf uns.

English translation:

тАЬBс╣Ыhaspati brings unto (the gods), after extricating them from the mountains, the cows that are theyielders of pure (milk), ever in motion, the objects of search and of desire, well-coloured and of unexceptionableform, (as men bring) barley from the granaries.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The cows: g─Бс╕е = the rain water;

Parvatebhyaс╕е = the clouds;from the granaries: sthivibhyaс╕е = kus─лdebhyaс╕е, usurers; nir ┼лpe = sows (as of seed)

Jamison Brereton

(The cowsтАФ) thoroughly civilized, providing for guests, vigorous, cherished, of lovely color and faultless formтАФ
Br╠еhaspati, having brought them through, strewed the cows forth from the mountains, like grain from sacks.

Griffith

Brhaspati, having won them from the mountains, strewed down, like barley out of winnowing- baskets,
The vigorous, wandering cows who aid the pious, desired of all, of blameless form, well-coloured.

Die vorw├дrts streben wandernd, munter eilend, die viel begehrten sch├╢n an Form und Farbe, Die K├╝he l├╢send von den Felsen, drosch sie Brihaspati hervor wie Korn aus Aehren.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSaturating (the earth) with water, scattering the receptacle of rain, the adorable Bс╣Ыhaspati, raising upthe cattle from the rock as (he raises) a meteor from the sky, rent the skin of the earth (with the hoofs of thecattle) as (Parjanya rends it) with rain.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Spraying the womb of truth with honey, flinging (it=honey?) down like a firebrand from heaven when the chant (sounded),
Br╠еhaspati, when he brought the cows up out of the stone, split asunder the skin of the earth as if (just) with water.

Griffith

As the Sun dews with meath the seat of Order, and casts a flaming meteor down from heaven.
So from the rock Brhaspati forced the cattle, and cleft the earth’s skin as it were with water.

Geldner

Die Wiege der Wahrheit, mit S├╝├Яigkeit besprengend wie der Wetterstrahl, der die Fackel des Himmels herabschleudert, hat Brihaspati, als er die K├╝he aus dem Fels herausholte, die Haut der Erde wie durch Wasserflut gespalten.

Grassmann

Des heil’gen Werkes Schooss mit Meth benetzend, und wie der Blitz des Himmels Fackel schleudernd, Die K├╝he holend aus dem Fels, zersprengte der Erde Haut Brihaspati wie Fluten.

English translation:

тАЬBс╣Ыhaspati drove away the darkness from the firmament with light as the wind (blows) the ┼Ъ─лp─Бlafrom the water; guessing (them to be there), he swept the Vala’s cows together to himself as the wind (sweeps)the clouds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъ─лp─Бla = an aquatic plural nt, ┼Ыaiv─Бla, the vallisneria

Jamison Brereton

With his light he drove away the darkness from the midspace as the wind drives the ┼Ы─лp─Бla-plant from the water.
Br╠еhaspati, having (just) stroked (the skin/womb) of Vala, as the wind does a cloud, brought the cows here as his own.

Griffith

Forth from mid air with light he dravc the darkness, as the gale blows a lily from the fiver.
Like the wind grasping at the cloud of Vala, Brhaspati gathered to himself the cattle,

Geldner

Mit Licht hat er die Finsternis aus dem Luftreich getrieben wie der Wind die Sipalapflanze aus dem Wasser. Brihaspati packte die K├╝he des Vala und trieb sie vor sich her wie der Wind die Wolke.

Grassmann

Durch Licht vertrieb das Dunkel aus der Luft er, so wie der Sturm die Binsen aus dem Wasser; Brihaspati, des Vala K├╝he fassend, trieb sie herbei wie Wind die Wetterwolke.

English translation:

тАЬWhen Bс╣Ыhaspati had discovered that name of the lowing kine in their plural ce in the cave, by his ownstrength he extricated the cattle from the rock as (breaking) the eggs of a bird (one extricates) the embryo.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For Br╠еhaspati brought to mind this very name of these who were resounding (with)in the seatтАФ(the name) that was hidden.
Having split the womb of the mountain like the eggs of a bird, he drove up the ruddy ones by himself.

Griffith

That secret name borne by the lowing cattle within the cave Brhaspati discovered,
And drave, himself, the bright kine from the mountain, like a bird’s young after the egg’s disclosure.

Geldner

Brihaspati gedachte n├дmlich des Namens dieser Lautbr├╝llenden, der an dem Orte verborgen war. Wie die Brut des Vogels, nachdem sie die Eier gespalten hat, so trieb er in eigner Person die K├╝he als die Brut des Berges heraus.

Grassmann

Brihaspati nahm wahr der K├╝he Wesen, der br├╝llenden, das in dem Sitz verborgne, Da knickte er des Geiers Brut wie Eier, und f├╝hrte aus dem Fels heraus die K├╝he.

English translation:

тАЬBс╣Ыhaspati looked round upon the cows shut up in the cave like fish in a dried up pool; he seized Valawith a shout, cutting him off like a bowl from a tree.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cows: madhu, honey; hence, Soma, or milk; here put for theyielders of milk

Jamison Brereton

He caught sight of the honey enclosed by the stone, like a fish living in shallow water.
He extracted it, like a (wooden) cup from a treeтАФBr╠еhaspati having cut apart (the mountain) with an (ear-)splitting cry.

Griffith

He looked around on rock-imprisoned sweetness as one who eyes a fish in scanty water.
Brhaspati, cleaving through with varied clamour, brought it forth like a bowl from out the timber.

Grassmann

Er sah das S├╝ss von dem Gestein umschlossen, gleich wie ein Fisch im seichten Wasser schmachtet; Er schuf’s heraus wie aus dem Holz den Becher, Brihaspati, den Fels mit Krachen spaltend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBс╣Ыhaspati found the dawn, the sun, Agni; he dispersed the gloom with light; he seized (the cattle fromthe rock)) of Vala surrounded by the kine as (one extracts) marrow from a bone.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He found the dawn, found the sun, found the fire; he thrust aside the dark shades with his chant [/ray].
Br╠еhaspati extracted (the cows) of Vala, whose beauty was the cows, like marrow from a joint.

Griffith

He found the light of heaven, and fire, and Morning: with lucid rays he forced apart the darkness.
As from a joint, Brhaspati took the marrow of Vala as he gloried in his cattle.

Geldner

Er fand die Usas, er die Sonne, er das Feuer; er vertrieb durch Zauberlied die Finsternis. Brihaspati holte die K├╝he des Vala, der mit den K├╝hen prunkte, wie das Mark aus dem Gelenk.

Grassmann

Er fand den Morgen, Himmelsglanz und Feuer, er jagte fort durch Licht die Finsternisse, Des Vala sch├╢ne K├╝he zog hervor dann Brihaspati wie Mark aus Pflanzenstengeln.

рд╣рд┐рдореЗрд╡ рдпрдерд╛ рд╣рд┐рдореЗрди рдкрд░реНрдгрд╛ рдкрд░реНрдгрд╛рдирд┐ рдкрджреНрдордкрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдореБрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рдореБрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рдирд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рджреНрд╡рд▓реЗрди рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рдирдиреАрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдЧреЛрдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ рдореБрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рдиреНрдпрднреВрд╡рдиреН ред рдЕрде рдЧрд╡рд╛рдордиреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдирд╛ рдЖрдЧрддреЗрди рд╣реЗрддреБрдирд╛ рд╡рд▓рдГ рдЕрдХреГрдкрдпрддреН рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рддрд╛ рдореБрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рдЧрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддреН ред рддрддреНрд░ рдЕрдирдиреБрдХреГрддреНрдпрдореН рдЕрдирдиреБрдХрд░рдгреАрдпрдореН рдЕрдкреБрдирдГ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдЪ рддрддреНрдХрд░реНрдо рдЪрдХрд╛рд░ ред рдпрдерд╛ рддрддреНрдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреНрдХрд░рдгреАрдпрдВ рди рднрд╡рддрд┐ рдпрдерд╛ рдкреБрдирд░рдХрд░рдгреАрдпрдВ рддрдерд╛рдХрд╛рд░реНрд╖реАрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рдХрд┐рдВ рддрджрд┐рддрд┐ рдЖрд╣ ред рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдорд╛рд╕рд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╕реМ рдорд┐рдердГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдорд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдпреЛрдГ рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд░рд╛рддрдГ рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд░рдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рддреН рддрдЪреНрдЪрдХрд╛рд░ ред рдпрд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╢реНрдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs the trees (bemoan) their leaves carried off by the winter, so Vala bemoaned his kine (carried off) byBс╣Ыhaspati; he did that which cannot be imitated, which cannot be repeated, whereby sun and moon mutually rise(day and night).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Trees: van─Бni = vanan─лy─Бni, the desirable wealth of cows; as leaves are carried off bywinter, so the desirable cows were carried off by Vala had pity on Bс╣Ыhaspati coming in search of the cows; i.e.,gave him the cows. He made this, i.e. the mutual rising of the sun and moon, which cannot be made afterwards,which cannot be made again

Jamison Brereton

As the woods (lament) their leaves stolen by cold, Vala lamented for the cows (stolen) by Br╠еhaspati.
He performed an inimitable (deed), not to be repeated as long as the sun and moon will rise in alternation.

Griffith

As trees for foliage robbed by winter, Vala mourned for the cows Brhaspati had taken.
He did a deed ne’er done, ne’er to be equalled, whereby the Sun and Moon ascend alternate.

Geldner

Wie die B├дume ihre vom Frost geraubten Bl├дtter, so vermi├Яte Vala die von Brihaspati geraubten K├╝he. Etwas Unnachahmbares hat er getan, das sich nicht wiederholt, solange Sonne und Mond abwechselnd aufgehen werden.

Grassmann

Wie B├дume, die durch Frost des Laubs beraubt sind, betrauert’ Vala die geraubten K├╝he; Brihaspati, was unnachahmlich, that er, dass Sonn’ und Mond in stetem Wechsel aufgehn.

Elizarenkova

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╣рд┐рдорд╛-рдЗрд╡ рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╣реЗрдордиреНрдд рдЛрддреБ рд╕реЗ рд╡рди рдореЗрдВ рд╣реЛрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдкрд░реНрдгрд╛ рдореБрд╖рд┐рддрд╛) рдкрддреНрддреЗ рдкреГрдердХреН рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рдЬрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЕрд▓рдЧ рд╣реЛ рдЬрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, (рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдирд╛) рд╡реЗрдж рдХрд╛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдХ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рд╡рд▓рдГ) рдЖрд╡рд░рдХ рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЛ рдкреГрдердХреН рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП (рдЧрд╛рдГ-рдЕрдХреГрдкрдпрддреН) рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдпрд╛рдБ-рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдПрдБ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рд░рдЪрддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН-рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдорд╛рд╕рд╛) рдЬрдм рддрдХ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛ (рдорд┐рдердГ-рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд░рд╛рддрдГ) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдореЗрдВ рджрд┐рди-рд░рд╛рдд рдпрд╛ рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ рдкрдХреНрд╖реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрджрдп рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ-рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдЧреЛрдЪрд░ рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рддрдм рддрдХ (рдЕрдирдиреБрдХреГрддреНрдпрдореН-рдЕрдкреБрдирдГ-рдЪрдХрд╛рд░) рдЙрд╕ рд╡реЗрджрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЛ, рдЬрд┐рд╕реЗ рдкреБрдирдГ-рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рдирд╣реАрдВ рдХрд░рддрд╛, рдПрдХ рдмрд╛рд░ рд╣реА рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезрежрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдФрд░ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛ рдХреЛ рддреЛ рджрд┐рди-рд░рд╛рдд рдореЗрдВ рдпрд╛ рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ рдкрдХреНрд╖реЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рдмрд╛рд░-рдмрд╛рд░ рдпрд╛ рдкреБрдирдГ-рдкреБрдирдГ рдЙрджрд┐рдд рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдкрд░рдиреНрддреБ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рд╕реЗ рдЫреБреЬрд╛рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдпрд╛ рд╡реЗрдж рдХреЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЛ рдПрдХ рдмрд╛рд░ рд╣реА рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдХреНрдпреЛрдВрдХрд┐ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХрд╛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╣реИред рдЙрд╕реЗ рдмрд╛рд░ рдмрд╛рд░ рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреА рдЖрд╡рд╢реНрдпрдХрддрд╛ рдирд╣реАрдВ реерезрежрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╣рд┐рдорд╛-рдЗрд╡ рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐ рдкрд░реНрдгрд╛ рдореБрд╖рд┐рддрд╛) рдпрдерд╛ рд╣рд┐рдореЗрди рд╣реЗрдордиреНрддреЗрди рд╡рдиреЗ рднрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ тАШрддрджреНрдзрд┐рддрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╕реНрдп рд▓реЛрдкрд╢реНрдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдГтАЩ рдкрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╡реГрдХреНрд╖реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдкреГрдердХреНрдХреГрддрд╛рдирд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ (рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдирд╛) рд╡реЗрджрд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрдГ тАШрдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рддреГрддреАрдпрд╛тАЩ (рд╡рд▓рдГ) рд╡рд▓рд╛рддреН-рдЖрд╡рд░рдХрд╛рджрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рджрд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рдкреГрдердХреНрдХрд░реНрддреНрддреБрдореН тАШрдкрдЮреНрдЪрдореАрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реА рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛тАЩ (рдЧрд╛рдГ-рдЕрдХреГрдкрдпрддреН) рд╡рд╛рдЪреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЬреАрд╡рддреНрдорднреНрдпрдГ рдЕрдХрд▓реНрдкрдпрддреН-рдЕрд░рдЪрдпрддреН тАЬрдХреГрдкрд╛ рдХреГрдкрддреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдХрд▓реНрдкрддреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛тАЭ [рдирд┐рд░реБреж ремредрео] (рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН-рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдорд╛рд╕рд╛ рдорд┐рдердГ-рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд░рд╛рддрдГ) рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╕реМ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдорд╛рддреН рдЙрджрдпрддрдГ-рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢реЗ-рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдпреЛрдГ рдкрдХреНрд╖рдпреЛрдГ-рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдЧреЛрдЪрд░реМ рднрд╡рддрдГ, рддрд╛рд╡рддреН (рдЕрдирдиреБрдХреГрддреНрдпрдореН-рдЕрдкреБрдирдГ-рдЪрдХрд╛рд░) рддрдерд╛ рддрджреНрд╡реЗрджрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рдкреБрдирд░реНрди рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╕рдХреГрджреЗрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯреАрдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ реерезрежрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe protecting (deities) have decorated the heaven with constellations as (men decorate) a brownhorse with golden trappings; they established darkness in the night and light in the day; Bс╣Ыhaspati fractured therock and recovered the cows.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Protecting deities: pitс╣Ыs, or progenitors, the Aс╣Еgirasas, who appear to have beenamong the ancient astronomers, the inventors of the lunar asterisms (nakс╣гatras)

Jamison Brereton

Like a dusky horse with pearls, the Fathers ornamented the heaven with stars.
In the night they placed darkness and light in the day. Br╠еhaspati split the rock and found the cows.

Griffith

Like a dark steed adorned with pearl, the Fathers have decorated heaven With constellations.
They set the light in day, in night the darkness. Brhaspati cleft the rock and found the cattle.

Geldner

Die V├дter schm├╝ckten den Himmel mit den Gestirnen aus wie einen Rappen mit Perlen. Die Finsternis verlegten sie auf die Nacht, auf den Tag das Licht. Brihaspati spaltete den Fels, er hat die K├╝he gefunden.

Grassmann

Den Himmel schm├╝ckten mit Gestirn die V├дter, gleich wie das schwarze Ross mit Edelsteinen; Zum Tag das Licht, zur Nacht das Dunkel f├╝gend; Brihaspati brach Felsen, fand die K├╝he.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWe have offered this homage to Bс╣Ыhaspati, who lives in mid-heaven, who recites in order many(sacred stanzas); may he bestow upon us food, with cows, with horses, with son, with dependants.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This act of reverence here we have performed for the one belonging to the storm cloud, who keeps bellowing after the many (cows?):
Br╠еhaspatiтАФfor he shall confer vigor on us with cows, with horses, with heroes, with superior men.
Sumitra V─Бdhrya┼Ыva is said to be the composer of the next two hymns (69тАУ70), one to Agni, one an ─Аpr─л hymn.

Griffith

This homage have we.offered to the Cloud God who thunders out to many in succession.
May this Brhaspati vouchsafe us fulness of life with kine and horses, men, and heroes.

Geldner

Diese Verbeugung haben wir dem wetterwolkengleichen Brihaspati gemacht, der in vielen Stimmen dem Donner nachbr├╝llt. So m├╢ge uns denn Brihaspati durch K├╝he, Rosse, er durch S├╢hne und Mannen Kraft verleihen.

Grassmann

Wir haben dies Gebet dem Wolkensohne gemacht, der vielen K├╝hen br├╝llend zujauchzt, Brihaspati verleihe uns durch Rinder, durch Rosse, M├дnner, Helden, Jugendst├дrke.

  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрднреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдп-рдЗрджрдВ рдирдордГ-рдЕрдХрд░реНрдо) рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдгреА рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдП рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдЧрдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ (рдпрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реАрдГ-рдЕрдиреБ-рдЖрдиреЛрдирд╡реАрддрд┐) рдЬреЛ рдкреБрд░рд╛рддрди-рд╢рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рддрд┐рдХ рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рднрд▓реА рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдкреНрд░рд╡рдЪрди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рд╕рдГ-рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ-рд╣рд┐) рд╡реЗрдж рдХрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рд╡рд╣ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдЧреЛрднрд┐рдГ) рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ (рд╕рдГ-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╢реАрд▓ рдорди рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдЪрд┐рддреНрддрд╛рд╣рдВрдХрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рд╕рдГ-рд╡реАрд░реЗрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд╣ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЛрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ (рд╕рдГ-рдиреГрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд╣ рд░рдХреНрддрд╡рд╛рд╣рдХ рдирд╛реЬрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ (рдирдГ-рд╡рдпрдГ-рдзрд╛рддреН) рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рдЬреАрд╡рди рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезреирее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдгреА рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╡реЗрджрд╡рдХреНрддрд╛ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рдирдорд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░-рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдЧрдд рдЖрджрд┐ рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдПред рдЙрд╕ рд╡реЗрджрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд╢рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рддрд┐рдХ рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИред рд╡рд╣ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдорди рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рдЪрд┐рддреНрдд рдЕрд╣рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЛрдВ, рд░рдХреНрддрдирд╛реЬрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╢рд╛рд░реАрд░рд┐рдХ рдЬреАрд╡рди рдФрд░ рдЖрдзреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорд┐рдХ рдЬреАрд╡рди рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерезреирее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрднреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдп-рдЗрджрдВ рдирдордГ-рдЕрдХрд░реНрдо) рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдп тАЬрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд╛-рдЕрднреНрд░рд┐рдГтАЭ [рд╢реж ремредрекредреоредрел] рдЦрд▓реНрд╡рд┐рджрдВ рдирдордГ рдХреБрд░реНрдордГ (рдпрдГ-рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реАрдГ-рдЕрдиреБ-рдЖрдиреЛрдирд╡реАрддрд┐) рдпрдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛рддрдиреАрдГ рд╢рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рддреАрдГ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдГ рдкрд░рдореНрдкрд░рдпрд╛ рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╡рдХреНрддрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╡реАрддрд┐ тАЬрдиреЛрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ-рднреГрд╢рдВ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдпрдиреНрддреЗтАЭ [рдЛреж рекредреиреиредрек рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдГ] (рд╕рдГ-рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ-рд╣рд┐) рд╕ рд╣рд┐ рд╡реЗрджрдкрддрд┐рдГ (рдЧреЛрднрд┐рдГ) рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпреИрдГ (рд╕рдГ-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдирд╢реАрд▓реИрд░реНрдордиреЛрднрд┐рд░рдиреНрддрдГрдХрд░рдгреИрдГ (рд╕рдГ-рд╡реАрд░реЗрднрд┐рдГ) рд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреИрдГ тАЬрдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛ рд╡реИ рджрд╢ рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГтАЭ [рд╢реж резреиредреоредрезредрезреи] (рд╕рдГ-рдиреГрднрд┐рдГ) рд░рдХреНрддрдиреЗрддреНрд░реАрднрд┐рд░реНрдирд╛рдбреАрднрд┐рдГ (рдирдГ-рд╡рдпрдГ-рдзрд╛рддреН) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдЬреАрд╡рдирдВ рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ реерезреирее
